This page contains general information about the [[Graphics processing unit|GPUs]] and video cards by [[Advanced Micro Devices]] (AMD), including those by [[ATI Technologies]] before 2006, based on official specifications in table form.
{{toclimit|3}}

== DirectX version note ==
[[DirectX]] version indicates which graphics acceleration operations the card implements.
* DirectX 6.0 - [[Texture mapping|Multitexturing]]
* DirectX 7.0 - Hardware [[Transform|Transformation, Clipping and Lighting]] (TCL/T&L)
* DirectX 8.0 - Pixel [[Shader]] 1.1 & Vertex Shader 1.1
* DirectX 8.1 - Pixel Shader 1.4 & Vertex Shader 1.1
* DirectX 9.0 - Shader Model 2.0
* DirectX 9.0b - Pixel Shader 2.0b & Vertex Shader 2.0
* DirectX 9.0c - Shader Model 3.0, [[GPGPU]]
* DirectX 9.0L - [[Windows Vista]] only, DirectX 9.0c, Shader Model 3.0, Windows Graphics Foundation 1.0, [[DXVA]] 1.0, [[GPGPU]]
* Direct3D 10.0 - Windows Vista/Windows 7, [[Unified shader model|Shader Model 4.0]], Windows Graphics Foundation 2.0, DXVA 2.0, [[GPGPU]]
* Direct3D 10.1 - Windows Vista SP1/Windows 7, Shader Model 4.1, Windows Graphics Foundation 2.1, DXVA 2.1, [[GPGPU]]
* Direct3D 11.0 - Windows Vista/[[Windows 7]], Shader Model 5.0, Tessellation, Multithreaded rendering, Compute shaders, implemented by hardware and software running Direct3D 9/10/10.1, [[GPGPU]]
* Direct3D 11.1 - [[Windows 8]], Stereoscopic 3D Rendering, [[GPGPU]]
* Direct3D 11.2 - Windows 8.1, Tiled resources, [[GPGPU]]
* Direct3D 12.0 - [[Windows 10]], low-level [[Rendering (computer graphics)|rendering]] [[Application programming interface|API]], [[GPGPU]]

== OpenGL version note ==
[[OpenGL]] version indicates which graphics acceleration operations the card implements.
* OpenGL 1.1 - Texture objects
* OpenGL 1.2 - 3D textures, BGRA and [[packed pixel]] formats<ref name='Gamedev1929'>{{cite news |first=Dave |last=Astle |title=Moving Beyond OpenGL 1.1 for Windows |date=2003-04-01 |url=http://www.gamedev.net/reference/articles/article1929.asp |work=gamedev.net |accessdate=2007-11-15}}</ref>
* OpenGL 1.3 - [[Texture mapping|Multitexturing]], multisampling, texture compression
* OpenGL 1.4 - Depth textures
* OpenGL 1.5 - Vertex Buffer Object (VBO), Occlusion Queries<ref name="OpenGLSpec">[http://www.opengl.org/documentation/specs/version2.1/glspec21.pdf OpenGL 2.1 specification]</ref>
* OpenGL 2.0 - [[GLSL]] 1.1, [[Multiple Render Targets|MRT]], Non Power of Two textures, [[Point Sprites]], Two-sided stencil<ref name="OpenGLSpec"/>
* OpenGL 2.1 - [[GLSL]] 1.2, Pixel Buffer Object (PBO), sRGB Textures<ref name="OpenGLSpec"/>
* OpenGL 3.0 - [[GLSL]] 1.3, Texture Arrays, Conditional rendering, Frame Buffer Object (FBO)<ref name="OpenGL3Spec">http://www.opengl.org/registry/doc/glspec30.20080811.pdf OpenGL 3.0 specification. Retrieved August 12, 2008.</ref>
* OpenGL 3.1 - [[GLSL]] 1.4, Instancing, Texture Buffer Object, Uniform Buffer Object, Primitive restart <ref>[http://www.opengl.org/registry/doc/glspec31.20090528.pdf OpenGL 3.1 specification. Retrieved October 1, 2009.]</ref>
* OpenGL 3.2 - [[GLSL]] 1.5, Geometry Shader, Multi-sampled textures <ref>[http://www.opengl.org/registry/doc/glspec32.core.20090803.pdf OpenGL 3.2 specification. Retrieved October 1, 2009.]</ref>
* OpenGL 3.3 - [[GLSL]] 3.30 Backports as much function as possible from the OpenGL 4.0 specification
* OpenGL 4.0 - [[GLSL]] 4.00 Tessellation on GPU, shaders with 64-bit precision
* OpenGL 4.1 - [[GLSL]] 4.10 Developer-friendly debug outputs, compatibility with OpenGL ES 2.0
* OpenGL 4.2 - [[GLSL]] 4.20 Shaders with atomic counters, draw transform feedback instanced, shader packing, performance improvements
* OpenGL 4.3 - [[GLSL]] 4.30 Compute shaders leveraging GPU parallelism, shader storage buffer objects, high-quality ETC2/EAC texture compression, increased memory security, a multi-application robustness extension
* OpenGL 4.4 - [[GLSL]] 4.40 Buffer Placement Control, Efficient Asynchronous Queries, Shader Variable Layout, Efficient Multiple Object Binding, Streamlined Porting of Direct3D applications, Bindless Texture Extension, Sparse Texture Extension
* OpenGL 4.5 - [[GLSL]] 4.50

== Video codec acceleration ==
* '''R100''' - [[Video Immersion]]
* '''R200''' - [[Video Immersion|Video Immersion II]]
* '''R300''' - [[Video Immersion|Video Immersion II]] + [[Video Shader]]
* '''R410''' - [[Video Shader|Video Shader HD]]
* '''R420''' - [[Video Shader|Video Shader HD]] + [[DXVA]]
* '''R520''' - [[Avivo|Avivo Video]]
* '''R600''' - [[Avivo|Avivo HD Video]] - [[Unified Video Decoder|UVD]]
* '''R700''' - UVD 2, UVD 2.2
* '''Evergreen''' - UVD 2.2
* '''Northern Islands''' - UVD 3 (HD 67xx UVD 2.2)
* '''Southern Islands''' - UVD 3, [[Video Codec Engine]]
* '''Volcanic Islands''' - UVD 4.x, [[Video Codec Engine 2.0]]<ref>http://www.tweakpc.de/hardware/tests/cpu/amd_a10-7850k_a10-7700k/s06.php</ref><ref>http://www.hitechreview.com/it-products/pc/amd%E2%80%99s-kaveri-chips-to-significantly-boost-performance/45507/</ref>

== Field explanations ==
The fields in the table listed below describe the following:
* '''Model''' – The marketing name for the processor assigned by ATi. Note that the ATi trademark has been replaced by AMD trademark starting with the Radeon HD 6000 series graphics processing units. Professional graphics processing units will switch to the AMD trademark as well.<ref>{{cite web |last=Wasson |first=Scott |title=AMD jettisons ATI brand name, makes Radeon its own |url=http://techreport.com/discussions.x/19547 |publisher=The Tech Report |accessdate=9 January 2011}}</ref>
* '''Launch''' – Date of release for the processor.
* '''Model number''' – Mobility VPUs are based on technology from several technology families. ATi assigns codenames based on an "MXX" model string, which does not relate to the actual technological base of the processor (represented by the R-number). Additionally, ATi is the sole supplier for all Mobility Radeon parts. For this reason, except for the Mobility Radeon 2000 series, all Mobility processors are listed on the same table.
* '''Code name''' – The internal engineering codename for the processor (typically designated by an RNXX name where N is the series number and XX is the market segment for which the product is designed. Additionally, a codename may follow the RVNXX format where "V" typically signifies a processor intended for a mainstream or value market segment).
* '''Fab''' – Fabrication process. Average feature size of components of the processor.
* '''Bus interface''' – Bus by which the graphics processor is attached to the system (typically an expansion slot, such as [[Conventional PCI|PCI]], [[AGP]], or [[PCIe]]).
* '''Memory''' – The reference amount of memory used by the processor.
* '''Core clock''' – The reference core clock frequency (used as some manufacturers adjust clocks lower and higher, this number will always be that listed by ATi).
* '''Memory clock''' – The reference memory clock frequency (used as some manufacturers adjust clocks lower and higher, this number will always be that listed by ATi).
* '''Config core''' – The layout of the graphics pipeline, in terms of functional units. Over time the number, type and variety of functional units in the GPU core has changed significantly; before each section in the list there is an explanation as to what functional units are present in each generation of processors.
* '''Performance subsection'''
** '''Shader operations''' - How many operations the pixel shaders (or unified shaders in DirectX 10 and newer GPUs) can perform. Measured in MOperations/s or GOperations/s.
** '''Pixel fillrate''' - The number of pixels the raster operators can render to a display in one second. Measured in MPixels/s or GPixels/s.
** '''Texture fillrate''' - The rate at which a texture can be mapped by the texture mapping units onto a polygon mesh in one second. Measured in MTextels/s or GTextels/s.
** '''Vertex operations''' - The amount of geometry operations that can be processed on the vertex shaders in one second (only applies to DirectX 9.0c and older GPUs). Measured in MVertices/s.
* '''Memory subsection'''
** '''Bandwidth''' – Maximum theoretical bandwidth for the processor at factory clock with factory bus width. GB=10<sup>9</sup> bytes.
** '''Bus type''' – Type of memory bus or buses utilized.
** '''Bus width''' – Maximum bit width of the memory bus or buses utilized. This will always be a factory bus width.
* '''API compliance section'''
** '''DirectX''' – Highest version of DirectX with which the hardware is fully compliant.
** '''OpenGL''' – Highest version of OpenGL with which the hardware is fully compliant.
* '''Features''' – Additional features that are not standard as a part of the two graphics libraries.

=== Radeon R500 (X1xxx) Series ===
{{Main|Radeon X1000 Series}}
** Note that ATI X1000 Series cards (e.g. X1900) don't have Vertex Texture Fetch, hence they do not fully comply with the VS 3.0 model. Instead, they offer a feature called "Render to Vertex Buffer (R2VB)" that provides functionality that is an alternative Vertex Texture Fetch.

=== Evergreen (HD 5xxx) Series ===
{{Main|Radeon HD 5000 Series|TeraScale (microarchitecture)#TeraScale 2|l2=TeraScale 2}}
* The HD5xxx series is the last series of AMD GPUs which supports two analogue [[Cathode ray tube|CRT]]-monitors with a single graphics card (i.e. with two RAM-DACs) [[AMD Eyefinity]] introduced.

=== {{anchor|Northern Islands (HD 6xxx) Series}}Radeon HD 6xxx Series ===

{{Reflist|group=N}}

==== IGP (HD 6xxx) ====
* All models include [[DirectX]] 11, [[OpenGL]] 4.4 and [[OpenCL]] 1.2
* All models feature the UNB/MC [[Computer bus|Bus]] [[I/O interface|interface]]
* All models do '''not''' feature double-precision FP
* All models feature Angle independent anisotropic filtering, UVD3, and [[AMD Eyefinity]] capabilities, with up to three outputs.
* All models feature 3D Blu-ray Disk acceleration.
* All models are based on [[TeraScale (microarchitecture)#TeraScale 3|TeraScale 2 (VLIW5)]]

=== {{anchor|Southern Islands (HD 7xxx) Series}}Radeon HD 7xxx Series ===
{{Main|Radeon HD 7000 Series|TeraScale (microarchitecture)#TeraScale 2|Graphics Core Next#GCN 1.0|l2=TeraScale 2 (VLIW5)|l3=Graphics Core Next}}
* All models up to including HD 76xx based on [[TeraScale (microarchitecture)#TeraScale 2|TeraScale 2 (VLIW5)]], HD 77xx - 79xx are based on [[Graphics Core Next#GCN 1.0|GCN 1.0]] (Graphics Core Next) architecture except the HD 7790 which is based on [[Graphics Core Next#GCN 1.1|GCN 1.1]]. 
* Only the Bonaire (GCN 1.1) based HD 7xx0-series supports OpenCL 2.0. GCN 1.0 devices do not support the complete OpenCL 2.0 profile at this time.<ref name="RN-WINLIN-OPENCL2-14.41">{{cite web |title=AMD OpenCL 2.0 Driver |url=http://support.amd.com/en-us/kb-articles/Pages/OpenCL2-Driver.aspx |website=support.amd.com/ |publisher=AMD |accessdate=2015-05-19 |ref=RN-WINLIN-OPENCL2-14.41}}</ref><ref name="system-requirements-driver-compatibility">{{cite web |title=MD5 Checksums, System Requirements & Driver Compatibility |url=http://developer.amd.com/tools-and-sdks/opencl-zone/amd-accelerated-parallel-processing-app-sdk/system-requirements-driver-compatibility/ |website=developer.amd.com/ |publisher=AMD |accessdate=2015-05-19 |ref=system-requirements-driver-compatibility}}</ref>
* GPUs based on the GCN (Graphics Core Next) architecture, all support Direct X 11.2 with the latest drivers (Initially came with DirectX 11.1 support) and also support the Mantle API.
* HD 7790 model is designed more like the 7800/7900 models rather than the 7700 featuring 2x primitive rate instead of 1x which is found in the other 7700 cards.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.extremetech.com/gaming/151367-amd-launches-radeon-7790-meet-the-xbox-720s-gpu |title=AMD launches Radeon 7790: Meet the Xbox 720's GPU |publisher=ExtremeTech |date=2013-03-22 |accessdate=2013-11-10}}</ref>
* Bonaire is in the Caribbean Sea, Malta is in the Mediterranean Sea. These parts are reverse rebranded out of the Sea Island Series to appear in the 7000 Series in 2013.{{Clarify|date=September 2013}}
* Bonaire XT is the only card in the 7000 series to support True Audio.
* The HD 7990 "Malta" was discontinued few months after its release.
* According to AMD CodeXL, HD 7990's code name is New Zealand.
* HD 7790 Caution: In Windows XP (Clean DirectX 9) the Performance (GFlop) is lower than a HD4770 (960 GFlops){{Or|date=May 2015}}

==== IGP (HD 7xxx) ====
* All models include [[DirectX]] 11, [[OpenGL]] 4.4 and [[OpenCL]] 1.2
* All models feature the UNB/MC [[Computer bus|Bus]] [[I/O interface|interface]]

=== {{anchor|Sea Islands (HD 8xxx) Series}}Radeon HD 8xxx Series ===
{{Main|Radeon HD 8000 Series|TeraScale (microarchitecture)#TeraScale 2|Graphics Core Next#GCN 1.0|l2=TeraScale 2 (VLIW5)|l3=Graphics Core Next}}

* All models up to including HD 84xx based on [[TeraScale (microarchitecture)#TeraScale 2|TeraScale 2 (VLIW5)]], HD 85xx and later are based on [[Graphics Core Next]] architecture.
* HD 8570 & HD 8670 will now feature 256&nbsp;KB L2 read/write cache<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.amd.com/US/PRODUCTS/DESKTOP/GRAPHICS/8000/Pages/8670.aspx#2 |title=AMD Radeon HD 8670 GPU |publisher=Amd.com |date=2012-10-26 |accessdate=2013-11-10}}</ref>
* all non-OEM versions are shifted into Q4' 13<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.3dcenter.org/news/amd-bringt-keine-neuen-desktop-grafikkarten-vor-dem-vierten-quartal |title=AMD bringt keine neuen Desktop-Grafikkarten vor dem vierten Quartal |publisher=3DCenter.org |language=de |date=2013-02-09 |accessdate=2013-11-10}}</ref>

<sup>1</sup> [[Unified shader model|Unified Shaders]] : [[Texture mapping unit|Texture Mapping Units]] : [[Render output unit|Render Output Units]]
<br /><sup>2</sup> Pixel fillrate is calculated as the number of '''ROP'''s multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>3</sup> Texture fillrate is calculated as the number of '''TMU'''s multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>4</sup> Single precision performance is calculated as two times the number of shaders multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>5</sup> Double precision performance of '''Hawaii''' is 1/8 of single precision performance,<ref name="tomshardware.com">[http://www.tomshardware.com/reviews/radeon-r9-290x-hawaii-review,3650.html Radeon R9 290X Review AMD's Back In Ultra-High-End Gaming - Hawaii A 6.2 Billion Transistor GPU For Gaming] "We've also come to learn that AMD changed the double-precision rate from 1/4 to 1/8 on the R9 290X, yielding a maximum .7 TFLOPS. The FirePro version of this configuration will support full-speed (1/2 rate) DP compute, giving professional users an incentive to spring for Hawaii's professional implementation."</ref> '''Tahiti''' is 1/4 of single precision performance, '''others 28&nbsp;nm chip''' is 1/16 of single precision performance.
<br /><sup>6</sup> Base clock of '''R9 290''' and '''R9 290X''' will maintain at 947&nbsp;MHz and 1000&nbsp;MHz before reaching 95&nbsp;°C, respectively.<ref name="ReferenceA">[http://www.tomshardware.com/reviews/radeon-r9-290-review-benchmark,3659.html AMD Radeon R9 290 Review Fast And $400, But Is It Consistent - Digging Deeper Into Hawaii’s Behavior]</ref>
<br /><sup>7</sup> The R9 285 utilizes loss-less colour compression which can increase effective memory performance (relative to GCN 1.0 and 1.1 cards) in certain situations.<ref name="extremetech.com">http://www.extremetech.com/gaming/189034-amd-radeon-r9-285-review-the-gcn-1-2-torpedo-that-takes-out-nvidias-gtx-760</ref><ref name="hexus.net">http://hexus.net/tech/reviews/graphics/74033-sapphire-radeon-r9-285-dual-x-oc-28nm-tonga/</ref>
<br /><sup>8</sup> Support for OpenCL 2.0 has been extended to the 200 Series' R7 and R9 models.<ref name="RN-WINLIN-OPENCL2-14.41"/>

=== {{anchor|Rx 3xx Series}}Radeon Rx 3xx Series ===
{{Main|AMD Radeon Rx 200 Series|Graphics Core Next#GCN 1.2|l2=Graphics Core Next}}

All GPUs are rebrands of Rx 2xx chips. <ref>http://www.amd.com/en-us/products/graphics/desktop/oem/r9#3</ref> <ref>http://www.amd.com/en-us/products/graphics/desktop/oem/r7#3</ref> <ref>http://www.amd.com/en-us/products/graphics/desktop/oem/r5#3</ref> <ref>http://www.techpowerup.com/212258/a</ref>

<sup>1</sup> [[Unified shader model|Unified Shaders]] : [[Texture mapping unit|Texture Mapping Units]] : [[Render output unit|Render Output Units]]
<br /><sup>2</sup> Pixel fillrate is calculated as the number of '''ROP'''s multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>3</sup> Texture fillrate is calculated as the number of '''TMU'''s multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>4</sup> Single precision performance is calculated as two times the number of shaders multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>5</sup> Double precision performance is 1/16 of single precision performance.
<br /><sup>6</sup> The R9 380 utilizes loss-less colour compression which can increase effective memory performance (relative to GCN 1.0 and 1.1 cards) in certain situations.<ref name="extremetech.com">http://www.extremetech.com/gaming/189034-amd-radeon-r9-285-review-the-gcn-1-2-torpedo-that-takes-out-nvidias-gtx-760</ref><ref name="hexus.net">http://hexus.net/tech/reviews/graphics/74033-sapphire-radeon-r9-285-dual-x-oc-28nm-tonga/</ref>

=== {{anchor|Pirate Islands (Rx 4xx) Series}}Radeon Rx 4xx Series ===
{{Main|AMD Radeon Rx 300 Series|Graphics Core Next#GCN 1.2|l2=Graphics Core Next}}
{{unreferenced section|date=December 2014}}

* Radeon R9 470: Trinidad (Curaçao/Pitcairn)
* Radeon R9 460: Tobago (Bonaire)
* Radeon R7 450X, R7 440 and R5 440X: Oland
* Radeon R5 410: Caicos

<br /><sup>1</sup> [[Unified shader model|Unified Shaders]] : [[Texture mapping unit|Texture Mapping Units]] : [[Render output unit|Render Output Units]]
<br /><sup>2</sup> Pixel fillrate is calculated as the number of '''ROP'''s multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>3</sup> Texture fillrate is calculated as the number of '''TMU'''s multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>4</sup> Single precision performance is calculated as two times the number of shaders multiplied by the base core clock speed.
<br /><sup>5</sup> Double precision performance of '''Hawaii''' is 1/8 of single precision performance,<ref name="tomshardware.com"/> '''Tahiti''' is 1/4 of single precision performance, '''others 28&nbsp;nm chip''' is 1/16 of single precision performance.

==== IGP (HD 6xxx) ====
* All models include [[DirectX]] 11, [[OpenGL]] 4.4 and [[OpenCL]] 1.2
* All models feature the UNB/MC [[Computer bus|Bus]] [[I/O interface|interface]]
* All models do '''not''' feature double-precision FP
* All models feature Angle independent anisotropic filtering, UVD3, and [[AMD Eyefinity|Eyefinity]] capabilities, with up to three outputs.
* All models are based on the VLIW5 architecture.

==== IGP (HD 6xxxG) ====
* All models include [[DirectX]] 11, [[OpenGL]] 4.4 and [[OpenCL]] 1.2
* All models feature the UNB/MC [[Computer bus|Bus]] [[I/O interface|interface]]
* All models do not feature double-precision FP
* All models feature Angle independent anisotropic filtering, UVD3 and [[AMD Eyefinity|Eyefinity]] capabilities, with up to three outputs.
* All models feature VLIW5

=== Radeon Rx M2xx Series ===
{{Main|AMD Radeon Rx 200 Series#Mobile}}

While the desktop versions are code-named "Sea Islands", the mobile GPUs of the AMD Radeon Rx 200 Series are code-named "Crystal Series": "Vesuvius", "Topaz" and "Amethyst".
